10&#160;mTorr or 1 Pa), moderate pressure (&#8776;1&#160;Torr or 100 Pa), atmospheric pressure (760&#160;Torr or 100 kPa)</li>\n<li>The degree of ionisation within the plasma&#8212;fully, partially, or weakly ionized</li>\n<li>The temperature relationships within the plasma&#8212;thermal plasma (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle T_{e}=T_{i}=T_{gas}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>e</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>g</mi>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mi>s</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle T_{e}=T_{i}=T_{gas}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="T_e = T_i = T_{gas}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/559abad0312505020e0fadd7bdc671e2d12896fc" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:14.73ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>), non-thermal or "cold" plasma (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle T_{e}\\gg T_{i}=T_{gas}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>e</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8811;<!-- &#8811; --></mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>g</mi>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mi>s</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle T_{e}\\gg T_{i}=T_{gas}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="T_e \\gg T_i = T_{gas}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/485dd6e8a33089d7998697ef5884d77d7052f760" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:15.245ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>)</li>\n<li>The electrode configuration used to generate the plasma</li>\n<li>The magnetization of the particles within the plasma&#8212;magnetized (both ion and electrons are trapped in <a href="/wiki/Gyroradius" title="Gyroradius">Larmor orbits</a> by the magnetic field), partially magnetized (the electrons but not the ions are trapped by the magnetic field), non-magnetized (the magnetic field is too weak to trap the particles in orbits but may generate <a href="/wiki/Lorentz_force" title="Lorentz force">Lorentz forces</a>)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Generation_of_artificial_plasma">Generation of artificial plasma</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Simple_representation_of_a_discharge_tube_-_plasma.png"><img alt="Simple representation of a discharge tube - plasma.png" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="249" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Simple_representation_of_a_discharge_tube_-_plasma.png/220px-Simple_representation_of_a_discharge_tube_-_plasma.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Simple_representation_of_a_discharge_tube_-_plasma.png/330px-Simple_representation_of_a_discharge_tube_-_plasma.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3e/Simple_representation_of_a_discharge_tube_-_plasma.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Simple_representation_of_a_discharge_tube_-_plasma.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Plasma_jacobs_ladder.jpg"><img alt="Artificial plasma produced in air by a Jacob\'s Ladder" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1762" data-file-width="2642" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Plasma_jacobs_ladder.jpg/220px-Plasma_jacobs_ladder.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Plasma_jacobs_ladder.jpg/330px-Plasma_jacobs_ladder.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Plasma_jacobs_ladder.jpg/440px-Plasma_jacobs_ladder.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Plasma_jacobs_ladder.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Artificial plasma produced in air by a <a href="/wiki/Spark_gap#Visual_entertainment" title="Spark gap">Jacob\'s Ladder</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Just like the many uses of plasma, there are several means for its generation, however, one principle is common to all of them: there must be energy input to produce and sustain it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hippler_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hippler-64">[64]</a></sup> For this case, plasma is generated when an <a href="/wiki/Electric_current" title="Electric current">electric current</a> is applied across a <a href="/wiki/Dielectric_gas" title="Dielectric gas">dielectric gas</a> or fluid (an electrically <a href="/wiki/Electrical_conductor" title="Electrical conductor">non-conducting</a> material) as can be seen in the adjacent image, which shows a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Discharge_tube" title="Discharge tube">discharge tube</a> as a simple example (<a href="/wiki/Direct_current" title="Direct current">DC</a> used for simplicity).\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Potential_difference" title="Potential difference">potential difference</a> and subsequent <a href="/wiki/Electric_field" title="Electric field">electric field</a> pull the bound electrons (negative) toward the <a href="/wiki/Anode" title="Anode">anode</a> (positive electrode) while the <a href="/wiki/Cathode" title="Cathode">cathode</a> (negative electrode) pulls the nucleus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chen_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chen-65">[65]</a></sup> As the <a href="/wiki/Voltage" title="Voltage">voltage</a> increases, the current stresses the material (by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_polarization" title="Electric polarization">electric polarization</a>) beyond its <a href="/wiki/Dielectric_strength" title="Dielectric strength">dielectric limit</a> (termed strength) into a stage of <a href="/wiki/Electrical_breakdown" title="Electrical breakdown">electrical breakdown</a>, marked by an <a href="/wiki/Electric_spark" title="Electric spark">electric spark</a>, where the material transforms from being an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insulator_(electrical)" title="Insulator (electrical)">insulator</a> into a <a href="/wiki/Electrical_conductor" title="Electrical conductor">conductor</a> (as it becomes increasingly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ionized" title="Ionized">ionized</a>). The underlying process is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Townsend_avalanche" title="Townsend avalanche">Townsend avalanche</a>, where collisions between electrons and neutral gas atoms create more ions and electrons (as can be seen in the figure on the right). The first impact of an electron on an atom results in one ion and two electrons. Therefore, the number of charged particles increases rapidly (in the millions) only "after about 20 successive sets of collisions",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leal-Quiros_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leal-Quiros-66">[66]</a></sup> mainly due to a small mean free path (average distance travelled between collisions).\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_arc">Electric arc</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cascade-process-of-ionization.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="617" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="265" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Cascade-process-of-ionization.svg/220px-Cascade-process-of-ionization.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Cascade-process-of-ionization.svg/330px-Cascade-process-of-ionization.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Cascade-process-of-ionization.svg/440px-Cascade-process-of-ionization.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cascade-process-of-ionization.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cascade process of ionisation. Electrons are "e&#8722;", neutral atoms "o", and cations "+".</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Townsend_Discharge.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="311" data-file-width="476" decoding="async" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Townsend_Discharge.svg/300px-Townsend_Discharge.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Townsend_Discharge.svg/450px-Townsend_Discharge.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Townsend_Discharge.svg/600px-Townsend_Discharge.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Townsend_Discharge.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Avalanche effect between two electrodes. The original ionisation event liberates one electron, and each subsequent collision liberates a further electron, so two electrons emerge from each collision: the ionising electron and the liberated electron.</div></div></div>\n<p>With ample current density and ionisation, this forms a luminous <a href="/wiki/Electric_arc" title="Electric arc">electric arc</a> (a continuous electric discharge similar to <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">lightning</a>) between the electrodes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[Note 1]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrical_resistance" title="Electrical resistance">Electrical resistance</a> along the continuous electric arc creates <a href="/wiki/Heat" title="Heat">heat</a>, which dissociates more gas molecules and ionises the resulting atoms (where degree of ionisation is determined by temperature), and as per the sequence: <a href="/wiki/Solid" title="Solid">solid</a>-<a href="/wiki/Liquid" title="Liquid">liquid</a>-<a href="/wiki/Gas" title="Gas">gas</a>-plasma, the gas is gradually turned into a thermal plasma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[Note 2]</a></sup> A thermal plasma is in <a href="/wiki/Thermal_equilibrium" title="Thermal equilibrium">thermal equilibrium</a>, which is to say that the temperature is relatively homogeneous throughout the heavy particles (i.e. atoms, molecules and ions) and electrons. This is so because when thermal plasmas are generated, <a href="/wiki/Electrical_energy" title="Electrical energy">electrical energy</a> is given to electrons, which, due to their great mobility and large numbers, are able to disperse it rapidly and by <a href="/wiki/Elastic_collision" title="Elastic collision">elastic collision</a> (without energy loss) to the heavy particles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gomez_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gomez-68">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[Note 3]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Examples_of_industrial.2Fcommercial_plasma"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Examples_of_industrial/commercial_plasma">Examples of industrial/commercial plasma</span></h3>\n<p>Because of their sizable temperature and density ranges, plasmas find applications in many fields of research, technology and industry. For example, in: industrial and extractive <a href="/wiki/Metallurgy" title="Metallurgy">metallurgy</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gomez_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-Gomez-68">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sza&#322;atkiewicz_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sza&#322;atkiewicz-71">[68]</a></sup> surface treatments such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plasma_spraying" title="Plasma spraying">plasma spraying</a> (coating), <a href="/wiki/Etching" title="Etching">etching</a> in microelectronics,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRC_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-NRC-72">[69]</a></sup> metal cutting<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nemchinsky_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nemchinsky-73">[70]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Welding" title="Welding">welding</a>; as well as in everyday <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_emissions_control" title="Vehicle emissions control">vehicle exhaust cleanup</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fluorescent_lamp" title="Fluorescent lamp">fluorescent</a>/<a href="/wiki/Electroluminescence" title="Electroluminescence">luminescent</a> lamps,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hippler_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hippler-64">[64]</a></sup> fuel ignition, while even playing a part in <a href="/wiki/Scramjet" title="Scramjet">supersonic combustion engines</a> for <a href="/wiki/Aerospace_engineering" title="Aerospace engineering">aerospace engineering</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peretich_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Peretich-74">[71]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Low-pressure_discharges">Low-pressure discharges</span></h4>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Glow_discharge" title="Glow discharge">Glow discharge</a> plasmas</i>: non-thermal plasmas generated by the application of DC or low frequency RF (&lt;100&#160;kHz) electric field to the gap between two metal electrodes. Probably the most common plasma; this is the type of plasma generated within <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fluorescent_light" title="Fluorescent light">fluorescent light</a> tubes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[72]</a></sup></li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Capacitively_coupled_plasma" title="Capacitively coupled plasma">Capacitively coupled plasma</a> (CCP)</i>: similar to glow discharge plasmas, but generated with high frequency RF electric fields, typically <a href="/wiki/ISM_band" title="ISM band">13.56&#160;MHz</a>. These differ from glow discharges in that the sheaths are much less intense. These are widely used in the microfabrication and integrated circuit manufacturing industries for plasma etching and plasma enhanced chemical vapor deposition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[73]</a></sup></li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Cascaded_Arc_Plasma_Source" title="Cascaded Arc Plasma Source">Cascaded Arc Plasma Source</a></i>: a device to produce low temperature (&#8776;1eV) high density plasmas (HDP).</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Inductively_coupled_plasma" title="Inductively coupled plasma">Inductively coupled plasma</a> (ICP)</i>: similar to a CCP and with similar applications but the electrode consists of a coil wrapped around the chamber where plasma is formed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[74]</a></sup></li>\n<li><i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Wave_heated_plasma&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Wave heated plasma (page does not exist)">Wave heated plasma</a></i>: similar to CCP and ICP in that it is typically RF (or microwave). Examples include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Helicon_discharge" title="Helicon discharge">helicon discharge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electron_cyclotron_resonance" title="Electron cyclotron resonance">electron cyclotron resonance</a> (ECR).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[75]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Atmospheric_pressure">Atmospheric pressure</span></h4>\n<ul><li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arc_discharge" title="Arc discharge">Arc discharge</a>:</i> this is a high power thermal discharge of very high temperature (&#8776;10,000 K). It can be generated using various power supplies. It is commonly used in <a href="/wiki/Metallurgy" title="Metallurgy">metallurgical</a> processes. For example, it is used to smelt minerals containing Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> to produce <a href="/wiki/Aluminium" title="Aluminium">aluminium</a>.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Corona_discharge" title="Corona discharge">Corona discharge</a>:</i> this is a non-thermal discharge generated by the application of high voltage to sharp electrode tips. It is commonly used in <a href="/wiki/Ozone" title="Ozone">ozone</a> generators and particle precipitators.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Dielectric_barrier_discharge" title="Dielectric barrier discharge">Dielectric barrier discharge</a> (DBD):</i> this is a non-thermal discharge generated by the application of high voltages across small gaps wherein a non-conducting coating prevents the transition of the plasma discharge into an arc. It is often mislabeled \'Corona\' discharge in industry and has similar application to corona discharges. It is also widely used in the web treatment of fabrics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[76]</a></sup> The application of the discharge to synthetic fabrics and plastics functionalizes the surface and allows for paints, glues and similar materials to adhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[77]</a></sup> The dielectric barrier discharge was used in the mid-1990s to show that low temperature atmospheric pressure plasma is effective in inactivating bacterial cells.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[78]</a></sup> This work and later experiments using mammalian cells led to the establishment of a new field of research known as <a href="/wiki/Plasma_medicine" title="Plasma medicine">plasma medicine</a>. The dielectric barrier discharge configuration was also used in the design of low temperature plasma jets. These plasma jets are produced by fast propagating guided ionisation waves known as plasma bullets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[79]</a></sup></li>\n<li><i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Capacitive_discharge&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Capacitive discharge (page does not exist)">Capacitive discharge</a>:</i> this is a <a href="/wiki/Nonthermal_plasma" title="Nonthermal plasma">nonthermal plasma</a> generated by the application of RF power (e.g., <a href="/wiki/ISM_band" title="ISM band">13.56&#160;MHz</a>) to one powered electrode, with a grounded electrode held at a small separation distance on the order of 1&#160;cm. Such discharges are commonly stabilized using a noble gas such as helium or argon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[80]</a></sup></li>\n<li>"<a href="/wiki/Piezoelectric_direct_discharge_plasma" title="Piezoelectric direct discharge plasma">Piezoelectric direct discharge plasma</a>:" is a <a href="/wiki/Nonthermal_plasma" title="Nonthermal plasma">nonthermal plasma</a> generated at the high-side of a piezoelectric transformer (PT). This generation variant is particularly suited for high efficient and compact devices where a separate high voltage power supply is not desired.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="MHD_converters">MHD converters</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Magnetohydrodynamic_converter" title="Magnetohydrodynamic converter">magnetohydrodynamic converter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magnetohydrodynamic_generator" title="Magnetohydrodynamic generator">magnetohydrodynamic generator</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Magnetohydrodynamic_drive" title="Magnetohydrodynamic drive">magnetohydrodynamic drive</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Electrothermal_instability" title="Electrothermal instability">Electrothermal instability</a></div>\n<p>A world effort was triggered in the 1960s to study <a href="/wiki/Magnetohydrodynamic_converter" title="Magnetohydrodynamic converter">magnetohydrodynamic converters</a> in order to bring <a href="/wiki/Magnetohydrodynamic_generator" title="Magnetohydrodynamic generator">MHD power conversion</a> to market with commercial power plants of a new kind, converting the <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_energy" title="Kinetic energy">kinetic energy</a> of a high velocity plasma into <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">electricity</a> with no <a href="/wiki/Moving_parts" title="Moving parts">moving parts</a> at a high <a href="/wiki/Efficiency" title="Efficiency">efficiency</a>. Research was also conducted in the field of supersonic and hypersonic aerodynamics to study plasma interaction with magnetic fields to eventually achieve passive and even active <a href="/wiki/Flow_control_(fluid)" title="Flow control (fluid)">flow control</a> around vehicles or projectiles, in order to soften and mitigate <a href="/wiki/Shock_wave" title="Shock wave">shock waves</a>, lower thermal transfer and reduce <a href="/wiki/Drag_(physics)" title="Drag (physics)">drag</a>.\n</p><p>Such ionized gases used in "plasma technology" ("technological" or "engineered" plasmas) are usually <i>weakly ionized gases</i> in the sense that only a tiny fraction of the gas molecules are ionized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[81]</a></sup> These kinds of weakly ionized gases are also nonthermal "cold" plasmas. In the presence of magnetics fields, the study of such magnetized nonthermal weakly ionized gases involves <a href="/wiki/Magnetohydrodynamics#Ideal_and_resistive_MHD" title="Magnetohydrodynamics">resistive magnetohydrodynamics</a> with low <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_Reynolds_number" title="Magnetic Reynolds number">magnetic Reynolds number</a>, a challenging field of plasma physics where calculations require <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dyadic_tensor" title="Dyadic tensor">dyadic tensors</a> in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/N-dimensional_space" title="N-dimensional space">7-dimensional</a> <a href="/wiki/Phase_space" title="Phase space">phase space</a>. When used in combination with a high <a href="/wiki/Hall_effect" title="Hall effect">Hall parameter</a>, a critical value triggers the problematic <a href="/wiki/Electrothermal_instability" title="Electrothermal instability">electrothermal instability</a> which limited these technological developments.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research<span id="Fields_of_active_research"></span></span></h2>\n<p>Plasmas are the object of study of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academic_field" title="Academic field">academic field</a> of <i>plasma science</i> or <i>plasma physics</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[82]</a></sup> including sub-disciplines such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_plasma_physics" title="Space plasma physics">space plasma physics</a>. It currently involves the following fields of active research and features across many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academic_journals" title="Academic journals">journals</a>, whose interest includes:\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:auto;"><tbody><tr>\n<td style="text-align: stability</a></li>\n<li>Plasma interactions with waves and beams</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Guiding_center" title="Guiding center">Guiding center</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Adiabatic_invariant" collision">Coulomb collision</a></li></ul></li>\n<li>Plasmas in nature\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Astrophysical_plasma" title="Astrophysical plasma">Astrophysical plasma</a></li>\n<li><a barrier discharge</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Enhanced_oil_recovery" title="Enhanced oil recovery">Enhanced oil recovery</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fusion_power" title="Fusion power">Fusion power</a>\n<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magnetic_fusion_energy" title="Magnetic fusion energy">Magnetic fusion energy</a> (MFE)&#160;&#8212;\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Tokamak" title="Tokamak">Tokamak</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stellarator" title="Stellarator">Stellarator</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Reversed_field_pinch" title="Reversed field pinch">Reversed field pinch</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Magnetic_mirror" title="Magnetic mirror">Magnetic mirror</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dense_plasma_focus" title="Dense plasma focus">Dense plasma focus</a></li></ul></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Inertial_confinement_fusion" title="Inertial confinement fusion">Inertial confinement fusion</a> (ICF)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Plasma_weapon" ashing</a></li>\n<li>Food processing\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Nonthermal_plasma" title="Nonthermal plasma">Nonthermal plasma</a> or "cold plasma"</li></ul></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" acceleration</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Plasma_medicine" title="Plasma medicine">Plasma medicine</a> (e. g. Dentistry<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tws44_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-tws44-86">[83]</a></sup>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Plasma_window" title="Plasma window">Plasma window</a></li></ul></li></ul>\n<p>\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_examples">Research examples</span></h2>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:30px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HallThruster_2.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="533" decoding="async" height="90" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/HallThruster_2.jpg/120px-HallThruster_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/HallThruster_2.jpg/180px-HallThruster_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/HallThruster_2.jpg/240px-HallThruster_2.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hall_effect_thruster" title="Hall effect thruster">Hall effect thruster</a>. The electric field in a plasma <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Double_layer_(plasma)" title="Double layer (plasma)">double layer</a> is so effective at accelerating ions that electric fields are used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ion_drive" title="Ion drive">ion drives</a>.\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n<div style="background: #ececec; color: #2C2C2C; vertical-align: middle; font-size: smaller; text-align: center;">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-67"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-67">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The material undergoes various "regimes" or stages (e.g. saturation, breakdown, glow, transition and thermal arc) as the voltage is increased under the voltage-current relationship. The voltage rises to its maximum value in the saturation stage, and thereafter it undergoes fluctuations of the various stages; while the current progressively increases throughout.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leal-Quiros_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-Leal-Quiros-66">[66]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-69"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-69">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Across literature, there appears to be no strict definition on where the boundary is between a gas and plasma. Nevertheless, it is enough to say that at 2,000&#176;C the gas molecules become atomized, and ionized at 3,000 &#176;C and "in this state, [the] gas has a liquid like viscosity at atmospheric pressure and the free electric charges confer relatively high electrical conductivities that can approach those of metals."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gomez_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gomez-68">[67]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-70"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-70">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Note that non-thermal, or non-equilibrium plasmas are not as ionized and have lower energy densities, and thus the temperature is not dispersed evenly among the particles, where some heavy ones remain "cold".</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em;
